In what was a bad year for Republicans, who lost control of the House for the first time since the Civil War, Garfield had his closest congressional election, winning with only 57 percent of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>d<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965233.E2.80.93236Rutkow200634.E2.80.9335_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965233.E2.80.93236Rutkow200634.E2.80.9335-108"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minority_leader.3B_Hayes_presidency">Minority leader; Hayes presidency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Minority leader; Hayes presidency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the Democratic takeover of the House of Representatives in 1875, Garfield lost his chairmanship of the Appropriations Committee. The Democratic leadership in the House appointed Garfield as a Republican member of Ways and Means. With many of his leadership rivals defeated in the 1874 Democratic landslide, and Blaine elected to the Senate, Garfield was seen as the Republican <a href="/wiki/Floor_leader" title="Floor leader">floor leader</a> and the likely Speaker should the party regain control of the chamber.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERutkow200637.E2.80.9339_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERutkow200637.E2.80.9339-109"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As the 1876 presidential election approached, Garfield was loyal to the candidacy of Senator Blaine, and fought for the former Speaker's nomination at the <a href="/wiki/1876_Republican_National_Convention" title="1876 Republican National Convention">1876 Republican National Convention</a> in Cincinnati. When it became clear, after six ballots, that Blaine could not prevail, the convention nominated Ohio Governor <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">Rutherford B. Hayes</a>. Although Garfield had supported Blaine, he had kept good relations with Hayes, and wholeheartedly supported the governor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978398.E2.80.93400_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978398.E2.80.93400-110"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield had hoped to retire from politics after his term expired to devote himself full-time to the practice of law, but to help his party, he sought re-election, and won it easily that October. Any celebration was short lived, as Garfield's youngest son, Neddie, fell ill with <a href="/wiki/Whooping_cough" title="Whooping cough" class="mw-redirect">whooping cough</a> shortly after the congressional election, and soon died.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978401.E2.80.93405_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978401.E2.80.93405-111"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electoral_Commission_(United_States).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg/220px-Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg/330px-Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg/440px-Electoral_Commission_%28United_States%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="488" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electoral_Commission_(United_States).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Garfield (second from right in the row of commissioners just below the gallery) served on the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_States)" title="Electoral Commission (United States)">Electoral Commission</a> that decided the disputed 1876 presidential election. (Painting by <a href="/wiki/Cornelia_Adele_Strong_Fassett" title="Cornelia Adele Strong Fassett">Cornelia Adele Strong Fassett</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When Hayes appeared to have lost the presidential election the following month to Democrat <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Tilden" title="Samuel Tilden" class="mw-redirect">Samuel Tilden</a>, the Republicans launched efforts to reverse the result in Southern states where they held the governorship: South Carolina, Louisiana, and Florida. If Hayes won all three states, he would take the election by a single electoral vote. Grant asked Garfield to serve as a "neutral observer" in the recount in Louisiana. The observers soon recommended to the state electoral commissions that Hayes be declared the winner—Garfield recommended that the entire vote of <a href="/wiki/West_Feliciana_Parish,_Louisiana" title="West Feliciana Parish, Louisiana">West Feliciana Parish</a>, which had given Tilden a sizable majority, be thrown out. The Republican governors of the three states certified that Hayes had won their states, to the outrage of Democrats, who had the state legislatures submit rival returns, and threatened to prevent the counting of the electoral vote—under the Constitution, Congress is the final arbiter of the election. Congress then passed a bill establishing the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_Commission_(United_States)" title="Electoral Commission (United States)">Electoral Commission</a>, to determine the winner. Although he opposed the Commission, feeling that Congress should count the vote and proclaim Hayes victorious, Garfield was appointed to it over the objections of Democrats that he was too partisan. Hayes emerged the victor by a Commission vote of 8 to 7, with all eight votes being cast by Republican politicians or appointees of that party to the Supreme Court. As part of the deal whereby they recognized Hayes as president, Southern Democrats secured the removal of federal troops from the South, ending Reconstruction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965251.E2.80.93261Rutkow200640_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965251.E2.80.93261Rutkow200640-112"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Although a Senate seat would be disposed of by the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_General_Assembly" title="Ohio General Assembly">Ohio General Assembly</a> after the resignation of <a href="/wiki/John_Sherman_(Ohio)" title="John Sherman (Ohio)" class="mw-redirect">John Sherman</a> to become Treasury Secretary, Hayes needed Garfield's expertise to protect him from the agenda of a hostile Congress, and asked him not to seek it. Garfield, as the president's key legislator, gained considerable prestige and respect from his role.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERutkow200641_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERutkow200641-113"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> When Congress debated what became the <a href="/wiki/Bland-Allison_Act" title="Bland-Allison Act" class="mw-redirect">Bland-Allison Act</a>, to have the government purchase large quantities of silver and strike it into fully legal tender <a href="/wiki/Morgan_dollar" title="Morgan dollar">dollar coins</a>, Garfield fought against this deviation from the gold standard, but it was enacted over Hayes's veto in February 1878.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965261_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965261-114"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Garfield during this time purchased the property in <a href="/wiki/Mentor,_Ohio" title="Mentor, Ohio">Mentor</a> that reporters later dubbed Lawnfield,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978498_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978498-115"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and from which he would conduct the first successful <a href="/wiki/Front_porch_campaign" title="Front porch campaign">front porch campaign</a> for the presidency. Hayes suggested that Garfield run for governor in 1879, seeing that as a road that would likely put Garfield in the White House. Garfield preferred to seek election as senator, and devoted his efforts to seeing that Republicans won the 1879 election for the General Assembly, with the likely Democratic candidate the incumbent, <a href="/wiki/Allen_G._Thurman" title="Allen G. Thurman">Allen G. Thurman</a>. The Republicans swept the legislative elections. Rivals were spoken of for the seat, such as Secretary Sherman, but he had presidential ambitions (for which he sought Garfield's support), and other candidates fell by the wayside. Garfield was elected to the Senate by the General Assembly in January 1880, though his term was not to begin until March 4, 1881.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978442.E2.80.93447_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978442.E2.80.93447-116"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_career_and_other_activities">Legal career and other activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legal career and other activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Garfield was one of three attorneys who argued for the petitioners in the landmark Supreme Court case <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_parte_Milligan" title="Ex parte Milligan">Ex parte Milligan</a></i> in 1866. The petitioners were pro-Confederate northern men who had been found guilty and sentenced to death by a military court for treasonous activities. The case turned on whether the defendants should instead have been tried by a civilian court, and resulted in a ruling that civilians could not be tried before military tribunals while the civil courts were operating. The oral argument was Garfield's first court appearance. <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Black" title="Jeremiah Black" class="mw-redirect">Jeremiah Black</a> had taken him in as a junior partner a year before, and assigned the case to him in light of his highly regarded oratory skills. With the result, Garfield instantly achieved a reputation as a preeminent appellate lawyer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978270_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978270-117"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During Grant's first term, discontented with public service, Garfield pursued opportunities in the law, but declined a partnership offer when told his prospective partner was of "intemperate and licentious" reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978347_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978347-118"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1873, after the death of Chase, Garfield appealed to Grant to appoint Justice <a href="/wiki/Noah_H._Swayne" title="Noah H. Swayne" class="mw-redirect">Noah H. Swayne</a> as Chief Justice. Grant, however, appointed <a href="/wiki/Morrison_R._Waite" title="Morrison R. Waite" class="mw-redirect">Morrison R. Waite</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcFeely1981387.E2.80.93389.2C_392_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcFeely1981387.E2.80.93389.2C_392-119"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Garfield thought the <a href="/wiki/Public_Land_Survey_System#Railroad_land_grants" title="Public Land Survey System">land grants</a> given to expanding railroads to be an unjust practice; as well, he opposed some monopolistic practices by corporations, as well as the power sought by the workers' unions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978331_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978331-120"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield supported the proposed establishment of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_civil_service" title="United States civil service" class="mw-redirect">United States civil service</a> as a means of ridding officials of the annoyance of aggressive office seekers. He especially wished to eliminate the common practice whereby government workers, in exchange for their positions, were forced to <a href="/wiki/Kickback_(bribery)" title="Kickback (bribery)">kick back</a> a percentage of their wages as political contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978335.E2.80.93338_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978335.E2.80.93338-121"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1876, Garfield displayed his mathematical talent when he developed a trapezoid proof of the <a href="/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem" title="Pythagorean theorem">Pythagorean theorem</a>. His finding was placed in the <i>New England Journal of Education</i>. Mathematics historian William Dunham stated that Garfield's trapezoid work was "really a very clever proof".<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidential_election_of_1880">Presidential election of 1880</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Presidential election of 1880">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_nomination">Republican nomination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Republican nomination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1880_Republican_National_Convention" title="1880 Republican National Convention">1880 Republican National Convention</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A cartoon. Grant, on the right, is semi-kneeling while others kneel behind him. Garfield stands upright and receives a sword from Grant. Behind him are cheering throngs, and two men raise a flag in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg/325px-The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg" width="325" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg/488px-The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8c/The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg/650px-The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1173" data-file-height="763" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Appomattox_of_the_third_termers_-_unconditional_surrender.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Following Grant's defeat for the nomination <a href="/wiki/Puck_(magazine)" title="Puck (magazine)"><i>Puck</i> magazine</a> satirized <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a>'s surrender to him at Appomattox by depicting Grant giving up his sword to Garfield.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Having just been elected to the Senate with Sherman's support, Garfield entered the 1880 campaign season committed to Sherman as his choice for the Republican presidential nominee.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978454.E2.80.93455_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978454.E2.80.93455-123"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Even before the convention began, however, a few Republicans, including <a href="/wiki/Wharton_Barker" title="Wharton Barker">Wharton Barker</a> of Philadelphia, thought Garfield the best choice for the nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978454.E2.80.93455_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978454.E2.80.93455-123"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield denied any interest in the position, but the attention was enough to make Sherman suspicious of his lieutenant's ambitions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978456.E2.80.93457_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978456.E2.80.93457-124"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Besides Sherman, the early favorites for the nomination were Blaine and former president Grant, but several other candidates attracted delegates as well.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198117.E2.80.9319_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198117.E2.80.9319-125"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As the convention began, Senator <a href="/wiki/Roscoe_Conkling" title="Roscoe Conkling">Roscoe Conkling</a> of New York, the floor leader for the Grant forces (known as the <a href="/wiki/Stalwart_(politics)" title="Stalwart (politics)">Stalwart</a> faction), proposed that the delegates pledge to support the eventual nominee in the general election.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383-126"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> When three West Virginia delegates declined to be so bound, Conkling sought to expel them from the convention. Garfield rose to defend the men, giving a passionate speech in defense of their right to reserve judgement.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383-126"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The crowd turned against Conkling, and he withdrew the motion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAckerman200381.E2.80.9383-126"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The performance delighted Garfield's boosters, who now believed more than ever that he was the only man who could attract a majority of the delegates' votes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978464.E2.80.93465_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978464.E2.80.93465-127"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After speeches in favor of the other front-runners, Garfield rose to place Sherman's name in nomination; his nominating speech was well-received, but the delegates mustered little excitement for the idea of Sherman as the next president.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978466.E2.80.93469_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978466.E2.80.93469-128"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> The first ballot showed Grant leading with 304 votes and Blaine in second with 284; Sherman's 93 placed him in a distant third. Subsequent ballots quickly demonstrated a deadlock between the Grant and Blaine forces, with neither having the 379 votes needed for nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAckerman200396.E2.80.93101_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAckerman200396.E2.80.93101-129"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_McLain_Rusk" title="Jeremiah McLain Rusk">Jeremiah McLain Rusk</a>, a member of the Wisconsin delegation, and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison" title="Benjamin Harrison">Benjamin Harrison</a>, an Indiana delegate, sought to break the deadlock by shifting a few of the anti-Grant votes to a <a href="/wiki/Dark_horse" title="Dark horse">dark horse</a> candidate—Garfield.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978472.E2.80.93475_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978472.E2.80.93475-130"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield gained 50 votes on the 35th ballot, and the stampede began. Garfield protested to the other members of his Ohio delegation that he had not sought the nomination and had never intended to betray Sherman, but they overruled his objections and cast their ballots for him.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978475.E2.80.93477_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978475.E2.80.93477-131"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> In the next round of voting, nearly all of the Sherman and Blaine delegates shifted their support to Garfield, giving him 399 votes and the Republican nomination. Most of the Grant forces backed the former president to the end, creating a disgruntled Stalwart minority in the party.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAckerman2003110.E2.80.93114_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAckerman2003110.E2.80.93114-132"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> To obtain that faction's support for the ticket, former <a href="/wiki/Collector_of_the_Port_of_New_York" title="Collector of the Port of New York">New York customs collector</a> <a href="/wiki/Chester_A._Arthur" title="Chester A. Arthur">Chester A. Arthur</a>, a member of Conkling's <a href="/wiki/Political_machine" title="Political machine">political machine</a>, was chosen as the vice-presidential nominee and Garfield's running mate.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978480.E2.80.93481_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978480.E2.80.93481-133"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campaign_against_Hancock">Campaign against Hancock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Campaign against Hancock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1880RepublicanPoster.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/1880RepublicanPoster.png/220px-1880RepublicanPoster.png" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/1880RepublicanPoster.png/330px-1880RepublicanPoster.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/1880RepublicanPoster.png/440px-1880RepublicanPoster.png 2x" data-file-width="984" data-file-height="680" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1880RepublicanPoster.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Garfield-Arthur election poster</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1880" title="United States presidential election, 1880">United States presidential election, 1880</a></div>
<p>Despite including a Stalwart on the ticket, animosity between the Republican factions carried over from the convention, and Garfield traveled to New York to meet with party leaders there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978488.E2.80.93491_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978488.E2.80.93491-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> After convincing the Stalwart crowd to put aside their differences and unite for the coming campaign, Garfield returned to Ohio, leaving the active campaigning to others, as was traditional at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978498.E2.80.93500_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978498.E2.80.93500-135"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, the Democrats settled on their nominee, Major General <a href="/wiki/Winfield_Scott_Hancock" title="Winfield Scott Hancock">Winfield Scott Hancock</a> of Pennsylvania, a career military officer.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978488.E2.80.93491_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978488.E2.80.93491-134"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Hancock and the Democrats expected to carry the <a href="/wiki/Solid_South" title="Solid South">Solid South</a>, while much of the North was considered safe territory for Garfield and the Republicans; most of the campaign would involve a few close states, including New York and Indiana.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978501.E2.80.93502_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978501.E2.80.93502-136"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Garf_07-04-2008_02;10;53PM.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A large three-story house of wood and stone" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG/220px-Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG/330px-Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG/440px-Garf_07-04-2008_02%3B10%3B53PM.JPG 2x" data-file-width="883" data-file-height="613" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Garf_07-04-2008_02;10;53PM.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The house at Garfield's Lawnfield estate, from which he conducted his "<a href="/wiki/Front_porch_campaign" title="Front porch campaign">front porch campaign</a>"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Practical differences between the candidates were few, and Republicans began the campaign with the familiar theme of <a href="/wiki/Waving_the_bloody_shirt" title="Waving the bloody shirt">waving the bloody shirt</a>: reminding Northern voters that the Democratic Party was responsible for secession and four years of civil war, and that if they held power they would reverse the gains of that war, dishonor Union veterans, and pay Confederate veterans pensions out of the federal treasury.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClancy1958175.E2.80.93180_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClancy1958175.E2.80.93180-137"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> With fifteen years having passed since the end of the war, and Union generals at the head of both tickets, the bloody shirt was of diminishing value in exciting the voters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978493.E2.80.93494_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978493.E2.80.93494-138"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> With a few months to go before the election, the Republicans switched tactics to emphasize the <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariff</a>. Seizing on the Democratic platform's call for a "tariff for revenue only", Republicans told Northern workers that a Hancock presidency would weaken the tariff protection that kept them in good jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClancy1958232.E2.80.93233_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClancy1958232.E2.80.93233-139"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Hancock made the situation worse when, attempting to strike a moderate stance, he said "the tariff question is a local question".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978493.E2.80.93494_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978493.E2.80.93494-138"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The ploy proved effective in uniting the North behind Garfield.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978511.E2.80.93513_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978511.E2.80.93513-140"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> In the end, fewer than ten thousand votes separated the two candidates, but in the <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">Electoral College</a>, Garfield had an easy victory over Hancock, 214 to 155.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978510.E2.80.93511_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978510.E2.80.93511-141"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency.2C_1881">Presidency, 1881</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Presidency, 1881">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Garfield wears an informal frock coat suit and has one hand inserted into the front of the jacket." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg/170px-PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg" width="170" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg/255px-PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg/340px-PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="5385" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PresidentJamesAGarfieldStandingFacingLeft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President Garfield</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabinet_and_inauguration">Cabinet and inauguration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cabinet and inauguration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between his election and his inauguration, Garfield was occupied with assembling a cabinet that would establish peace between Conkling's and Blaine's warring factions. Blaine's delegates had provided much of the support for Garfield's nomination, and the Maine senator received the place of honor: Secretary of State.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978519.E2.80.93521_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978519.E2.80.93521-142"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine was not only the president's closest advisor, he was obsessed with knowing all that took place in the White House, and was even said to have spies posted there in his absence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978554.E2.80.93555_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978554.E2.80.93555-143"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield nominated <a href="/wiki/William_Windom" title="William Windom">William Windom</a> of Minnesota as Secretary of the Treasury, <a href="/wiki/William_H._Hunt" title="William H. Hunt">William H. Hunt</a> of Louisiana as Secretary of the Navy, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Todd_Lincoln" title="Robert Todd Lincoln">Robert Todd Lincoln</a> as Secretary of War, and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Kirkwood" title="Samuel J. Kirkwood">Samuel J. Kirkwood</a> of Iowa as Secretary of the Interior. New York was represented by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lemuel_James" title="Thomas Lemuel James">Thomas Lemuel James</a> as Postmaster General. Garfield appointed Pennsylvania's <a href="/wiki/Wayne_MacVeagh" title="Wayne MacVeagh">Wayne MacVeagh</a>, an adversary of Blaine's, as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_General" title="United States Attorney General">Attorney General</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198133.E2.80.9336_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198133.E2.80.9336-144"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine tried to sabotage the appointment by convincing Garfield to name an opponent of MacVeagh, <a href="/wiki/William_E._Chandler" title="William E. Chandler">William E. Chandler</a>, as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Solicitor_General" title="United States Solicitor General" class="mw-redirect">Solicitor General</a> under MacVeagh. Only Chandler's rejection by the Senate forestalled MacVeagh's resignation over the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978555.E2.80.93561_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978555.E2.80.93561-145"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Distracted by cabinet maneuvering, Garfield's inaugural address was not up to his typical oratorical standards.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965330_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECaldwell1965330-146"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> In one high point, Garfield emphasized the civil rights of <a href="/wiki/African-Americans" title="African-Americans" class="mw-redirect">African-Americans</a>, saying "Freedom can never yield its fullness of blessings so long as the law or its administration places the smallest obstacle in the pathway of any virtuous citizen."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978538.E2.80.93540_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978538.E2.80.93540-147"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> After discussing the gold standard, the need for education, and an unexpected denunciation of Mormon polygamy, the speech ended. The crowd applauded, but the speech, according to Peskin, "however sincerely intended, betrayed its hasty composition by the flatness of its tone and the conventionality of its subject matter."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978539_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978539-148"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Garfield's appointment of James infuriated Conkling, a factional opponent of the Postmaster General, who demanded a compensatory appointment for his faction, such as the position of Secretary of the Treasury. The resulting squabble occupied much of Garfield's brief presidency. The feud with Conkling reached a climax when the president, at Blaine's instigation, nominated Conkling's enemy, Judge <a href="/wiki/William_H._Robertson" title="William H. Robertson">William H. Robertson</a>, to be Collector of the Port of New York. This was one of the prize patronage positions below cabinet level, and was then held by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Atkins_Merritt" title="Edwin Atkins Merritt">Edwin A. Merritt</a>. Conkling raised the time-honored principle of <a href="/wiki/Senatorial_courtesy" title="Senatorial courtesy">senatorial courtesy</a> in an attempt to defeat the nomination, to no avail. Garfield, who believed the practice to be corrupt, would not back down and threatened to withdraw all nominations unless Robertson was confirmed, intending to "settle the question whether the President is registering clerk of the Senate or the Executive of the United States."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198138_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198138-149"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Ultimately, Conkling and his New York colleague, Senator <a href="/wiki/Thomas_C._Platt" title="Thomas C. Platt">Thomas C. Platt</a>, resigned their Senate seats to seek vindication, but found only further humiliation when the New York legislature elected others in their places. Robertson was confirmed as Collector and Garfield's victory was clear. To Blaine's chagrin, the victorious Garfield returned to his goal of balancing the interests of party factions, and nominated a number of Conkling's Stalwart friends to offices.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978572_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978572-150"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reforms">Reforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Reforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Left_Puck.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A cartoon. Garfield, in night clothes and slippers, is on the doorstep looking at an ugly crying baby in a basket on the ground." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Left_Puck.jpg/220px-Left_Puck.jpg" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Left_Puck.jpg/330px-Left_Puck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Left_Puck.jpg/440px-Left_Puck.jpg 2x" data-file-width="619" data-file-height="552" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Left_Puck.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An 1881 <i><a href="/wiki/Puck_(magazine)" title="Puck (magazine)">Puck</a></i> cartoon shows Garfield finding a baby at his front door with a tag marked "Civil Service Reform, compliments of <a href="/wiki/Rutherford_B._Hayes" title="Rutherford B. Hayes">R.B. Hayes</a>". Hayes, his predecessor in the presidency, is seen in the background dressed like a woman and holding a bag marked "R.B. Hayes' Savings, <a href="/wiki/Fremont,_Ohio" title="Fremont, Ohio">Fremont, Ohio</a>".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Grant and Hayes had both advocated civil service reform, and by 1881, civil service reform associations had organized with renewed energy across the nation. Garfield sympathized with them, believing that the <a href="/wiki/Spoils_system" title="Spoils system">spoils system</a> damaged the presidency and distracted from more important concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198139.E2.80.9341_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198139.E2.80.9341-151"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Some reformers were disappointed that Garfield had advocated limited tenure only to minor office seekers and had given appointments to his old friends, but many remained loyal and supported Garfield.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198139.E2.80.9341_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198139.E2.80.9341-151"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Corruption in the post office also cried out for reform. In April 1880, there had been a congressional investigation into corruption in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Post_Office_Department" title="United States Post Office Department">Post Office Department</a>, in which profiteering rings allegedly stole millions of dollars, securing bogus mail contracts on <a href="/wiki/Star_routes" title="Star routes">star routes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978578_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978578-152"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> After obtaining contracts with the lowest bid, costs to run the mail routes would be escalated and profits would be divided among ring members. That year, Hayes stopped the implementation of any new star route contracts. Shortly after taking office, Garfield received information from Attorney General MacVeagh and Postmaster General James of postal corruption by an alleged star route ringleader, Second Assistant Postmaster-General <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Brady" title="Thomas J. Brady">Thomas J. Brady</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978580_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978580-153"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield demanded Brady's resignation and ordered prosecutions that would end in trials for conspiracy. When told that his party, including his own campaign manager, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_W._Dorsey" title="Stephen W. Dorsey" class="mw-redirect">Stephen W. Dorsey</a>, was involved, Garfield directed MacVeagh and James to root out the corruption in the Post Office Department "to the bone", regardless of where it might lead.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978578_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeskin1978578-152"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Brady resigned and was eventually indicted for conspiracy. After two "star route" ring trials in 1882 and 1883, the jury found Brady not guilty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198194.E2.80.9395_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198194.E2.80.9395-154"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_rights_and_education">Civil rights and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Civil rights and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Garfield believed that the key to improving the state of African American civil rights would be found in education aided by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148-155"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> During Reconstruction, <a href="/wiki/Freedman" title="Freedman">freedmen</a> had gained citizenship and suffrage that enabled them to participate in government, but Garfield believed their rights were being eroded by Southern white resistance and illiteracy, and was concerned that blacks would become America's permanent "<a href="/wiki/Peasantry" title="Peasantry" class="mw-redirect">peasantry</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148.E2.80.9349_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148.E2.80.9349-156"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> His answer was to propose a "universal" education system funded by the federal government. Congress and the northern white public, however, had lost interest in African-American rights, and federal funding for universal education did not find support in Congress during Garfield's term.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148.E2.80.9349_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198148.E2.80.9349-156"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield also worked to appoint several African Americans to prominent positions: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, recorder of deeds in Washington; <a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Elliott" title="Robert B. Elliott">Robert Elliot</a>, special agent to the Treasury; <a href="/wiki/John_M._Langston" title="John M. Langston" class="mw-redirect">John M. Langston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haitian</a> minister; and <a href="/wiki/Blanche_K._Bruce" title="Blanche K. Bruce" class="mw-redirect">Blanche K. Bruce</a>, register to the Treasury. Garfield believed that Southern support for the Republican party could be gained by "commercial and industrial" interests rather than race issues and began to reverse Hayes's policy of conciliating Southern Democrats.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198149.E2.80.9350_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198149.E2.80.9350-157"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> He appointed <a href="/wiki/William_H._Hunt" title="William H. Hunt">William H. Hunt</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Carpetbagger" title="Carpetbagger">carpetbagger</a> Republican from Louisiana, as Secretary of the Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198149.E2.80.9350_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198149.E2.80.9350-157"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> To break the hold of the resurgent Democratic Party in the Solid South, Garfield took patronage advice from Virginia Senator <a href="/wiki/William_Mahone" title="William Mahone">William Mahone</a> of the biracial independent <a href="/wiki/Readjuster_Party" title="Readjuster Party">Readjuster Party</a>, hoping to add the independents' strength to the Republicans' there.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198150.E2.80.9353_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke198150.E2.80.9353-158"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policy_and_naval_reform">Foreign policy and naval reform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Foreign policy and naval reform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/170px-James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/255px-James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg/340px-James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1211" data-file-height="1453" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_G._Blaine_-_Brady-Handy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/James_G._Blaine" title="James G. Blaine">James G. Blaine</a>, Garfield's Secretary of State</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Entering the presidency, Garfield had little foreign policy experience, so he leaned heavily on Blaine. Blaine, a former <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">protectionist</a>, now agreed with Garfield on the need to promote freer trade, especially within the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364-159"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Their reasons were twofold: firstly, Garfield and Blaine believed that increasing trade with <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> would be the best way to keep Great Britain from dominating the region.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364-159"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Secondly, by encouraging exports, they believed they could increase American prosperity, and by doing so position the Republican party as the author of that prosperity, ensuring continued electoral success.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200062.E2.80.9364-159"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield authorized Blaine to call for a Pan-American conference in 1882 to mediate disputes among the Latin American nations and to serve as a forum for talks on increasing trade.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200065.E2.80.9366Doenecke198155.E2.80.9357_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200065.E2.80.9366Doenecke198155.E2.80.9357-160"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, they hoped to negotiate a peace in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> then being fought by <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200065.E2.80.9366Doenecke198155.E2.80.9357_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200065.E2.80.9366Doenecke198155.E2.80.9357-160"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Blaine favored a resolution that would not result in Peru yielding any territory, but Chile, which had by 1881 occupied the Peruvian capital, <a href="/wiki/Lima" title="Lima">Lima</a>, rejected any settlement that restored the previous <i>status quo</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200070Doenecke198157.E2.80.9358_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200070Doenecke198157.E2.80.9358-161"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield sought to expand American influence in other areas, calling for renegotiation of the <a href="/wiki/Clayton-Bulwer_Treaty" title="Clayton-Bulwer Treaty" class="mw-redirect">Clayton-Bulwer Treaty</a> to allow the United States to construct <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal" title="Panama Canal">a canal through Panama</a> without British involvement, as well as attempting to reduce British influence in the strategically located <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hawaii" title="Kingdom of Hawaii">Kingdom of Hawaii</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200074.E2.80.9380Peskin1978576.E2.80.93577_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200074.E2.80.9380Peskin1978576.E2.80.93577-162"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield's and Blaine's plans for the United States' involvement in the world stretched even beyond the Western Hemisphere, as he sought commercial treaties with <a href="/wiki/Joseon_Dynasty" title="Joseon Dynasty" class="mw-redirect">Korea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merina_Kingdom" title="Merina Kingdom">Madagascar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrapol200081Doenecke198171.E2.80.9373_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrapol200081Doenecke198171.E2.80.9373-163"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> Garfield also considered enhancing the United States' military strength abroad, asking Navy Secretary Hunt to investigate the condition of the navy with an eye toward expansion and modernization.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981145.E2.80.93147_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981145.E2.80.93147-164"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> In the end, these ambitious plans came to nothing after Garfield was assassinated. Nine countries had accepted invitations to the Pan-American conference, but the invitations were withdrawn in April 1882 after Blaine resigned from the cabinet and Arthur, Garfield's successor, cancelled the conference.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981130.E2.80.93131_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981130.E2.80.93131-165"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>e<span>]</span></a></sup> Naval reform continued under Arthur, if on a more modest scale than Garfield and Hunt had envisioned, ultimately ending in the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Squadron_of_Evolution" title="Squadron of Evolution">Squadron of Evolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981148.E2.80.93149_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoenecke1981148.E2.80.93149-167"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_cabinet">Administration and cabinet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_A._Garfield&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Administration and cabinet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jgarfield.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="Formal seated portrait in oils" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Jgarfield.jpeg/220px-Jgarfield.jpeg" width="220" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Jgarfield.jpeg/330px-Jgarfield.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Jgarfield.jpeg/440px-Jgarfield.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2411" data-file-height="3000" /></a>

</div>
